## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in mechanics of materials. Typical relationships include elastic stress–strain laws with temperature-dependent stiffness, thermal expansion (stress from constrained thermal strain), and temperature-softened plasticity/hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (small-strain solids with temperature-dependent modulus and thermal expansion)
- Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic regime, stiffness changes approximately linearly with T over a limited range)
- Polynomial modulus in temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (elastic modulus varying nonlinearly with T)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (strong temperature sensitivity of stiffness; c1 typically negative for softening)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (empirical nonlinear stress–strain curve, with T shifting the level)
- Ramberg–Osgood implicit-type (explicit rearrangement form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (nonlinear elastic/plastic transition; can be inverted numerically to sigma(epsilon))
- Ludwik/Hollomon-type with thermal offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**c4 (yield/flow stress plus strain hardening, both temperature-dependent)
- Thermal softening factor times strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * T)) (multiplicative decomposition into strain term and temperature softening term)
- Hyperelastic polynomial (small-to-moderate strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (captures nonlinearity in elastic response with T-dependent coefficients)
- Saturation-type hardening with temperature-dependent asymptote: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 + c3 * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon))) (hardening that approaches a plateau; T changes scale)
- Thermoelastic with separate thermal stress term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) (useful if there is pre-stress/thermal mismatch leading to nonzero sigma at epsilon=0)
- Piecewise yield-like elastic–plastic surrogate (smooth): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - c2 * log(c3 + exp(c4 * ((c5 + c6 * T) - (c7 + c8 * T) * epsilon))) (smooth approximation to elastic response capped by temperature-dependent flow behavior)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: if sigma/epsilon decreases with T, model E(T) via (c0 + c1*T), (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2), or c0*exp(c1*T) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal expansion under constraint: nonzero stress at epsilon=0 that varies with T suggests a term like (c0 + c1*T) * (epsilon - c2*(T-c3)) or an added thermal stress offset (c0 + c1*T).
- Elastic-to-plastic transition: curvature in sigma–epsilon that changes from steep to gentler slope can be captured with Ramberg–Osgood-type structures or sums of linear and power-law terms in epsilon.
- Strain hardening vs saturation: continuously increasing slope at large epsilon favors power-law epsilon**c; leveling-off at large epsilon favors (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or other asymptotic hardening terms.
- Thermal softening of flow stress: if the whole stress level drops with increasing T at fixed epsilon, use multiplicative softening factors in T (e.g., exp(c*T)) applied to a strain hardening term.
- Nonlinearity mainly at higher strain: if small-strain response is nearly linear but deviates later, include higher-order epsilon terms (epsilon**3, epsilon**c with c>1) with T-dependent coefficients.
- Sign/offset behavior: if sigma changes sign with T at fixed epsilon (e.g., due to mismatch), include a temperature-driven offset term plus an elastic term in epsilon.
- Different T-sensitivity at different strains: if T affects low-strain and high-strain regimes differently, let both the intercept/yield-like term and the hardening coefficient depend on T separately.
- Data suggests a transition near a characteristic temperature: if behavior changes sharply around some T0 (e.g., near a glass transition), use smooth transition functions in T (e.g., log(1+exp(c*(T-c0)))) multiplying elastic/hardening terms.

Structure desc      : Additive polynomial/power model with a T-modulated fractional-power term T·|ε|^c1, a T-linear baseline, a T·ε interaction, plus ε power-law (ε^c5), linear ε, constant, and a standalone |ε|^c1 term. T appears only linearly (no higher powers) and multiplies the |ε|^0.5976 and ε terms; ε appears via |ε|^0.5976, ε, and ε^1.5976. With c1≈0.598 and c5≈1.598 (non-integer), the dominant ε-dependence comes from large c4≈677 and c6≈615, while the large negative c8≈−778 partly offsets the |ε|^c1 contribution against T*c0*|ε|^c1 depending on T. Approximate form: (2.2747T−777.8)|ε|^0.598 + (−0.3507T) + (−1.6478T)ε + 677.3·ε^1.598 + 614.7ε + 105.5.

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci0)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
Candidate formulas: 52

GT (fixed) simplifies structurally to a sum of **three** parts, all sharing the same temperature shift \(T-T_0\) with \(T_0=316.1945018642116\):

\[
\text{GT}=
31.119982052994235\,\epsilon\Big(1-0.05295088673159155\,(T-T_0)\Big)\;-\;0.22554447458683766\,(T-T_0)\;+\;3.629301836816963\,\epsilon^{0.5975773894779193}(T-T_0)
\]

Expand to see the essential monomials in \(T\) and \(\epsilon\):

- A term \(A\,\epsilon\) (constant in \(T\))
- A term \(B\,\epsilon\,T\) (linear in \(T\) times \(\epsilon\))
- A term \(C\,T\) (linear in \(T\), independent of \(\epsilon\))
- A constant term \(D\) (independent of \(T,\epsilon\)) coming from \((T-T_0)\) expansions
- A term \(E\,\epsilon^{p}\,T\) with **non-integer exponent** \(p=0.5975773894...\)
- A term \(F\,\epsilon^{p}\) (from \(-(T_0)\epsilon^p\) when expanding \((T-T_0)\))

So any matching candidate must be able to represent simultaneously:
1) \(\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon T\) terms,
2) \(T\) and constant terms,
3) \(\epsilon^{p}T\) and \(\epsilon^{p}\) terms with the **same exponent \(p\)**,
and crucially **no \(T^2\)** terms and no nonlinear-in-\(T\) functions (log/exp/sin) unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Now check candidates.

---

### 1
Has terms: \(T| \epsilon|^{c1}\), \(T\), \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^{c5}\), \(\epsilon\), constant, and \(|\epsilon|^{c1}\).
It can create \(\epsilon^p T\) via \(T|\epsilon|^{c1}\) and \(\epsilon^p\) via \(|\epsilon|^{c1}\) (set \(c1=p\), assume \(\epsilon\ge 0\) so \(|\epsilon|^{c1}=\epsilon^{c1}\)). But it **cannot** create the needed **\(\epsilon T\)** and **\(\epsilon\)** with the correct independent coefficients while also matching the GT’s specific coupling structure? Actually it *does* have \(T*c3*\epsilon\) and \(c6*\epsilon\), so that part is possible. It also has \(T*c2\) and constant \(c7\). The problem: GT’s \(\epsilon^p\) term is tied to \((T-T_0)\), meaning coefficients of \(\epsilon^p T\) and \(\epsilon^p\) must be negatives scaled by the same \(T_0\): coefficient(\(\epsilon^p\)) = \(-T_0\)*coefficient(\(\epsilon^p T\)). Candidate 1 allows \(\epsilon^p T\) coefficient \(=c0\) and \(\epsilon^p\) coefficient \(=c8\) independently, so we *can* set \(c8=-T_0 c0\). So that constraint can be met. Similarly, GT’s pure \(T\) and constant are linked by \((T-T_0)\): constant term from that part must equal \(-T_0\)*coefficient(\(T\)) for the \(-0.2255(T-T_0)\) contribution, but candidate has independent \(T*c2\) and constant \(c7\), so we can set \(c7=-T_0 c2\) plus additional constants from other parts. Also GT’s \(\epsilon T\) and \(\epsilon\) coefficients are linked because \(31.11998\epsilon(1-0.05295(T-T_0))\) implies a specific relation between \(\epsilon T\) and \(\epsilon\) constant term; candidate has independent \(T*c3*\epsilon\) and \(c6*\epsilon\), so we can satisfy that too.
However, candidate 1 also includes an extra \(\epsilon^{c5}\) term \(c4\epsilon^{c5}\) that GT does **not** have unless we set \(c4=0\). That’s allowed.
So structurally candidate 1 **can** represent all needed monomials with correct linkages by choosing constants appropriately (and using \(\epsilon\ge 0\) to drop Abs).
=> Candidate 1 is a potential match.

But we must check one more thing: GT has **no standalone \(T\epsilon^p\) plus standalone \(\epsilon^p\)** beyond the shared \((T-T_0)\) factor; candidate can enforce that by setting \(c8=-T_0 c0\) as noted. So yes.

**Conclusion: Candidate 1 can match GT.**

---

### 2
Contains \(T^2 c0\). GT has no \(T^2\); must set \(c0=0\). Then it has \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\), \(T\), \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon\), constant, and \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\).
To match GT’s \(\epsilon^p\) with \(p\neq 2\), we can set \(c5=0\) to remove \(\epsilon^2\) term (by setting coefficient \(c5=0\)), and set \(c2=p\). Then same reasoning as candidate 1: can match. So 2 also could match.

---

### 3
Has \(T^2\) (kill with \(c0=0\)), has \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\), and a problematic \(T*c3*(c4+\epsilon)^{c5}\). GT does not have a shifted-power in \(\epsilon\) inside a \(T\) term. Only way is set \(c3=0\) to remove it. Then remaining terms include \(\epsilon^2\) etc; can set those coefficients to 0 and reduce to form similar to candidate 2. So it can match as well.

---

### 4
Form: \(T c0 \epsilon + T c1 + c2\epsilon^2 + c3\epsilon^{c4} + c5\epsilon + c6 + c7\epsilon^{c8}\).
No term of form \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with non-integer \(p\) unless \(T c0\epsilon\) could be that, but exponent is fixed 1. There is **no** \(T\epsilon^{c}\) with free exponent. So cannot produce \(\epsilon^{0.597...}T\).  
=> No match.

### 5
Same issue: no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with free exponent (only \(T c0\epsilon\)).  
=> No match.

### 6
Has \(T^2\) (set \(c0=0\)), has \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\) and also \(T*c3*(c4+\epsilon)^{c5}\) which must be removed by \(c3=0\). Then it lacks a standalone \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\) term needed to create the \(-T_0\) companion of \(\epsilon^p T\). Actually it *does* have \(c8|\epsilon|^{c2}\). Good. Also has only \(c6\epsilon\) (no \(T\epsilon\) term), so cannot match GT’s \(\epsilon T\) term.  
=> No match.

### 7
After setting \(c0=0\), it has \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\), \(T\), \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon\), constant, and \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\). This is essentially the needed basis (like candidate 1 but without extra \(\epsilon^{c}\) term). With \(\epsilon\ge 0\), set \(c2=p\), and enforce the \((T-T_0)\) linkage by choosing the constant \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\) coefficient appropriately.  
=> Match possible.

### 8
Has rational terms \(T*c3/(T*c4+c5)\) and \(c7/(T*c4+c5)\). GT has no such dependence; only removable if \(c3=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then it reduces to candidate 2/7 type (with \(T^2\) removable). So could match.  
=> Match possible.

### 9–13
All include \(T^2\) removable, and have \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\) plus \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\) and enough linear terms; any extra \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon^{c}\), or rational term can be zeroed by setting its coefficient to 0. These can be reduced to the same spanning set as candidate 7.  
=> Match possible for 9,10,11,12,13 (with appropriate zeroing of extra structures; for 12 also set \(c4=0\) to kill \(T^{c3}c4\) or set \(c4=0\)).

### 14–28
These are like candidate 1 but with extra sin/log/exp terms. Those can be removed by setting their coefficients to 0 (e.g., \(c4=0\)). Then they reduce to candidate 1-type and can match (provided they still have both \(T\epsilon\) and \(\epsilon\) and \(T\epsilon^p\) and \(\epsilon^p\); most do). Some (like 16) replace \(T*c2\) with \(T*c2*(c3+\epsilon)^{c4}\) which would need \(c2=0\) to remove, potentially losing the pure \(T\) term; but pure \(T\) is required. If the only pure \(T\) term is inside that shifted power, then it fails. Specifically:
- 16: \(T*c2*(c3+\epsilon)^{c4}\) is the only non-\(\epsilon^p\) \(T\) term besides \(T*c0|\epsilon|^{c1}\). If we set \(c2=0\) to remove it, we lose the needed pure \(T\) term. If we keep it, it introduces unwanted \(\epsilon\)-dependence in the pure \(T\) part. So 16 cannot match.
- 17: has an extra \(T*c4*(c5+\epsilon)^{c6}\) removable by \(c4=0\); then it’s like 14 and can match.
Others (14,15,18,20–28) can be reduced to candidate 1-type by zeroing the special function term (if present) and combining coefficients.
=> All match possible except 16 and 19 (19 has \(c5*\epsilon*(T+c6)^{c7}\) which cannot be made linear in \(T\) for all \(T\) unless \(c5=0\); then it reduces to 21-type which can match).

### 29
Has \(T^2\) removable, but its \(T\)-dependent \(\epsilon\) nonlinearity is \(T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)^{c3}\) (shifted). To get both a pure \(T\) term and a \(T\epsilon\) term from this, you’d need binomial expansion, which only works as a polynomial for integer \(c3\), and even then introduces higher powers unless \(c3=1\). If \(c3=1\), it becomes \(T*c1*(c2+\epsilon)=T*c1*c2 + T*c1*\epsilon\) which gives pure \(T\) and \(T\epsilon\), good. But still no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with \(p=0.597...\). The remaining \(\epsilon^{c5}\) and \(\epsilon^{c9}\) are not multiplied by \(T\). So cannot create \(\epsilon^p T\).  
=> No match.

### 30
Has \(T*c0\epsilon\), \(T*c1\), and \(T^{c2}c3\) (kill with \(c3=0\)), plus \(\epsilon^{c5}\) and \(\epsilon^{c9}\) not multiplied by \(T\). No \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with free exponent.  
=> No match.

### 31
Like 2/7 with extra \(\epsilon^2\); can zero it. Has both \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\) and \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\), plus \(T\), \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon\), constant.  
=> Match possible.

### 32–36, 39, 52
These have only \(T\epsilon\) and \(T\) linear terms, and \(\epsilon^{c}\) terms **not multiplied by \(T\)**. No \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with free exponent.  
=> No match.

### 37–45
These include exp/log/sin terms removable by setting their coefficients to 0, and otherwise have the same \(T|\epsilon|^{c2}\) + \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\) + linear terms structure (after also setting \(T^2\) coefficient to 0).  
=> Match possible.

### 46
Has \(T*c0\) (pure \(T\)), \(T*c1|\epsilon|^{c2}\) (gives \(\epsilon^p T\)), and \(|\epsilon|^{c2}\) (via \(c6|\epsilon|^{c2}\)), plus \(\epsilon\) and constant and \(\epsilon^2\) (zero it). But it lacks a \(T\epsilon\) term.  
=> No match.

### 47–49
No linear-in-\(T\) structure matching \((T-T_0)\) across multiple terms; 49 has exp(T*c5) multiplying \(|\epsilon|^{c6}\) which cannot be made linear in \(T\) for all \(T\) unless coefficient is 0, but then no \(T\epsilon^p\).  
=> No match.

### 50–51
50 has \(T^2\) and \(T\epsilon\) but no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with free exponent. 51 has \( \epsilon*(T+c6)^{c7}\) which cannot be forced to be exactly linear in \(T\) for all \(T\) unless \(c7=1\), but still gives \(\epsilon T\), not \(\epsilon^p T\).
